Voice
Mark Lewis Jones
Appearances
Dragon Age II
Veld
is a mercenary who works alongside his brother,
Mekel
.
Involvement
This section contains spoilers for:
Dragon Age II
.
Veld is involved in the quest
Gamlen's Greatest Treasure
. Upon visiting
Gamlen's House
, Hawke finds a letter directed to
Gamlen
regarding a valuable gem. Hawke, following up on the letter, ends up in
Darktown
in order to meet the sender. After arriving, Hawke finds Mekel and a group of mercenaries waiting for them. Mekel says that he was paid to deliver the letter but now wants the gem for himself. Hawke can try to convince Mekel that they do not possess the gem, but Mekel attacks Hawke nevertheless. After the battle, Hawke finds a letter on Mekel's person directing them to a place called The Sink. Once there, Hawke fights through multiple enemies until entering a large cavern. In this cavern, Hawke meets their long-lost cousin
Charade Amell
. While talking to Hawke, Veld will enter and explain that Mekel was his brother and that he wants the gem so his brother's death was not for nothing. Veld and a dozen mercenaries then attack Hawke and company. He is killed in the ensuing battle.
Quests
Gamlen's Greatest Treasure

Darkspawn

, his superior. After several armed deserters attack Ewald and are saved only by the intervention of the
Hawke
siblings and
Aveline Vallen
, Wright runs to the
courtyard
to investigate. He is quickly berated by Ewald for his delay.
If Hawke betrays
Athenril
by accepting
Cavril
's bribe, Wright removes her and her smugglers from the fortress.

Dragon Age: The Veilguard
Xenon the Antiquarian
is the owner of the
Black Emporium
, located
deep under the streets
of
Kirkwall
.
Background
Xenon is an ancient being who is almost 300 years old.
He was once a Kirkwall nobleman living in the
Steel Age
. Extremely wealthy, and equally arrogant, he believed that someone as high-ranking as himself should not have to succumb to death, and so spent many years and a large amount of his fortune in search of a way to live forever.
Eventually, he found an
Antivan
Witch of the Wilds
, and made a deal with her to attain eternal life. She granted him his wish, but he, unfortunately, forgot also to ask for eternal youth.
His body withered and decayed over the centuries. Xenon used his fortune in an attempt to preserve his body using mystical and dangerous means, but no method has ever been successful.
Finally no longer able to move on his own, he went into hiding in the
Undercity
and began collecting strange and rare artifacts. He extends invitations to his shop only to people he deems worthy—those who have enough money to fund his search for a cure against aging.
The many servants who take care of him still hunt to find a way to reverse the effects of aging and return him to his once youthful state.
Xenon is immobile and uses a magical artifact to imitate speech as he lost his ability to speak.
He sits in the center of his emporium and appears to have an excess of limbs. He is bathed hourly to keep his body from drying up.
Involvement
Dragon Age II
Xenon sends
Hawke
a
letter
at the beginning of Act 1, an invitation to the Black Emporium, along with instructions on navigating the Undercity to reach the shop and a charm that acts as a pass.
At Hawke's initial visit to the Black Emporium, Xenon is excited to have a customer. He keeps an urchin boy as his assistant, and a stone golem, Thaddeus Gigantus Crumbum the Third, provides security and theft protection. Xenon claims Thaddeus is his "favorite".
In each act, more of Xenon's artifacts become available in The Black Emporium to unlock codex entries, and Xenon adds new items to his inventories.
Dragon Age: Inquisition
Years later, Xenon extends an invitation to the
Inquisition
to come and partake of his wares. Though the golem does not seem to be present when
the Inquisitor
visits, they do encounter a miniaturized bear named Chauncey that Xenon has acquired from a
Magister
sometime in the past few years.
Xenon's servants have apparently been busy over the last few years acquiring many new artifacts and items, including
legendary crafting schematics
, and rare armor, weapons, and accessories.
Dragon Age: The Veilguard
Approximately 10 years after the closing of
The Breach
, Xenon extends an
invitation
to
Rook
to come and visit his emporium in
Dock Town
, located in
Minrathous
. The store is located next to the Elevator to the Docks and remains locked until an invite is received.

Waterlogged Note
Trivia
Xenon's story of immortality is likely based on
Tithonus
, the lover of the Greek Goddess
Eos
from Greek mythology. Eos asked
Zeus
to make Tithonus immortal but, like Xenon, forgot to ask for eternal youth. He then aged until he became nothing more than a grasshopper, which Eos kept in a box.
Xenon is referenced in BioWare's Anthem video game. The bar in Fort Tarsis was formerly named the Black Emporium and the current owner, Max, scarcely recalls her predecessor was named Xeno, who was struck by lightning.
His voice and some of his quotes resemble that and those of Darth Sidious, better known as Palpatine or the Evil Emperor from Star Wars. He seems to have a fascination with dark power and objects, hence also the Sith Crone similarities.
Xenon's Golem, Thaddeus Gigantus Crumbum the Third, is a reference to the animated television show "The Venture Bros.," whose main character is Dr. Thaddeus Venture. In the second season premier, which debuted in 2006, Dr. Venture's son Hank calls him a "crumbum" as an insult.
He is against the Red Templars finding his shop claiming "they'd just break everything".
Xenon has fed a Venatori visiting his shop to a monster living under the floorboards.
A bard claims to have seen Xenon at an auction house in
Llomerryn
.
Xenon is rumoured to send his urchins to
Dock Town
in
Minrathous
to buy valuable items. He is said to pay them well.

Appearances
Dragon Age II
Yevhen
is a
surface dwarf
merchant living in
Kirkwall
. He is also in good standing with the
Dwarven Merchants' Guild
. He is the father of
Merin
,
Emrys
, and
Iwan
, and the employer of
Dera
, an
elven
woman who raised his sons after his wife died.
Involvement
This section contains spoilers for:
Dragon Age II
.
Note:
Yevhen will only be encountered if a
Dragon Age: Origins
save where
Nathaniel Howe
died or was never recruited into the
Grey Wardens
was imported.
Yevhen is involved in the quest
Fool's Gold
. Yevhen desperately asks
Hawke
to retrieve his three sons who have gone down into the
Deep Roads
by themselves, in search of treasure. Once down there, Hawke will find Yevhen's eldest son, Emrys, sitting in front of a locked door. He will explain that his younger brother, Iwan, locked the youngest brother, Merin, in a room full of
darkspawn
before scampering off to find the treasure. Hawke then tells Emrys to go back to his father and must now choose which brother to save. If Hawke goes around the locked door and goes to the room Merin is locked in, Hawke and company must help him fight off a small troop of darkspawn. This act saves Merin, who then goes back to his father. However, doing this will result in Iwan's death. Alternatively, Hawke can bypass Merin's tomb and run straight to Iwan. Helping Iwan fight off his darkspawn will result in Merin's death.
Upon returning with only two sons, Yevhen is devastated. If Merin is the one who perished and Yevhen is told the truth (that Iwan locked him in a room full of darkspawn in order to get the treasure), Yevhen becomes enraged and banishes Iwan.
Quests

(conditional)
